### Post by james215 on 2016-04-08
Hello Everyone,

I have been browsing the internet for quite some time and can't seem to resolve my wifi issue.

I recently installed Ubuntu onto an old 32 bit Dell Latitude D610.The problem is that I can't connect to the internet over wifi. I can connect over Ethernet though.

When I click on the wifi button at the top of the screen, I can see a greyed out list of networks in the area. And whenever I click on the System Settings button and then the Network button, I can see my network's name in the list. However, whenever I click on my network I get an error that says:

"Authentication required by Wi-Fi network
Passwords or encryption keys are required to access the Wi-Fi network 'my_network's name'. "

So I never get a chance to even type in my network's password. I just get this message.

Any help in resolving this would be awesome. 

Thank you for taking time to read this,
James

---

### Post by coffeecat on 2016-04-08
I've moved this thread to the ***Networking & Wireless*** sub-forum, where you are more likely to get the help you need. Please read this sticky: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=370108](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=370108) - and follow the instructions to run the wireless script. That will provide information without which forum members will not be able to help.

### Post by grahammechanical on 2016-04-08
What does it mean? I will give it go.

> Kernel driver in use: airo 

That means there is a kernel driver for your WiFi adapter card and it is use. No kernel driver = no working WiFi adapter. But we already knew that because Network Manager was showing wireless access points including your own wireless access point (router). Therefore, the wireless adapter was working = switched on and a functioning driver.

Compare this
> eth0      Link encap:Ethernet  HWaddr <MAC 'eth0' [IF]>             inet addr:192.168.1.3  Bcast:192.168.1.255  Mask:255.255.255.0
          inet6 addr: fe80::<IP6 'eth0' [IF]>/64 Scope:Link
          UP BROADCAST RUNNING MULTICAST  MTU:1500  Metric:1
          RX packets:2561 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 frame:0
          TX packets:1757 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 carrier:0
          collisions:0 txqueuelen:1000 
          RX bytes:3205244 (3.2 MB)  TX bytes:200386 (200.3 KB)
          Interrupt:16 
with this
> wifi0     Link encap:UNSPEC  HWaddr <MAC 'wifi0' [IF]>  
          BROADCAST MULTICAST  MTU:2312  Metric:1
          RX packets:0 errors:307 dropped:0 overruns:0 frame:307
          TX packets:51 errors:51 dropped:0 overruns:0 carrier:0
          collisions:0 txqueuelen:100 
          RX bytes:0 (0.0 B)  TX bytes:7635 (7.6 KB)
          Interrupt:17 Base address:0xde00 

[FONT=arial]The absence of UP & RUNNING tells us that you are not connected to the router. That is confirmed by this
> 
wifi0     IEEE 802.11-DS  ESSID:""  
          Mode:Managed  Frequency:2.412 GHz  Access Point: Invalid   
          Bit Rate:11 Mb/s   Tx-Power=20 dBm   Sensitivity=0/65535  
          Retry limit:16   RTS thr:off   Fragment thr:off
          Power Management:off
          Link Quality=0/100  Signal level=-107 dBm  Noise level=-107 dBm
          Rx invalid nwid:3830  Rx invalid crypt:0  Rx invalid frag:0
          Tx excessive retries:0  Invalid misc:23304   Missed beacon:0

If you were connected to the router the name of your wireless access point would be inside the inverted commas of ESSID: " "

And then there is this
> 
State: connected (global)

- Device: eth1 -----------------------------------------------------------------
  Type:              802.11 WiFi
  Driver:            airo
  State:             disconnected
  Default:           no
  HW Address:        <MAC 'eth1' [IF]>

All of which is telling us what we already know. You have not made a WiFi connection with the router. And the reason? You need to authenticate the connection because the connection is encrypted with WPA2 encryption.

When you click on your WiFi access point you should be given a Dialog box where you can put in the WPA-PSK key. Also known as the wireless key or pass-phrase. Do you not get that dialog box? Strange.

Is there a Network Manager icon in the top panel. It should be 2 arrows going in opposite directions. Click on that and then select your wireless access point. Does that not give you a dialog labelled "Authentication required by WiFi network" with a panel for the password?

[/FONT]Regards

---

### Post by QLee on 2016-04-09
> **james215 said:**
> 
What does this awesomness mean? haha

One thing that I notice is the line in udev rules:

# PCI device 0x14b9:0xa504 (airo)
SUBSYSTEM=="net", ACTION=="add", DRIVERS=="?*", ATTR{address}=="<MAC 'eth1' [IF]>", ATTR{dev_id}=="0x0", ATTR{type}=="1", KERNEL=="eth*", NAME="eth1"

Now, this is the same hardware that the system seems to identify as wifi0, thus the system shows two WiFi cards when there is only one. I can imagine that might cause a problem.

Does it make any difference if you comment out that udev rules entry and reboot?

---

### Post by grahammechanical on 2016-04-09
> And whenever I click on the System Settings button and then the Network  button, I can see my network's name in the list. However, whenever I  click on my network I get an error that says:

To do it through System Settings you need to edit the connection and in the dialog box open the WiFi security tab and there is a panel where the wireless key or passphrase goes.

---

### Post by tripp98 on 2016-04-10
First simple thing to try.

plug in network cable.

in system settings
open software & updates
go to additional drivers tab.

see if there is a driver for your wireless card.  apply it if its there.  if not better people than I will have to assist

---

### Post by wildmanne39 on 2016-04-10
Please do:
```
echo "blacklist dell_laptop" | sudo tee -a /etc/modprobe.d/blacklist.conf
```
Reboot
Does it scan and connect now?
